**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox Necko Networking to NSS TLS Handshake Chain

## Your Task

Trace how Firefox initiates a TLS connection from the networking layer to the crypto layer. Find: 1. The C++ source file in `netwerk/protocol/http/` that creates an SSL transport for HTTPS connections (look for `nsHttpConnection` or `TLSFilterTransaction`). 2. The file in `netwerk/socket/` that defines the `nsSSLIOLayerHelpers` class which bridges Necko to NSS. 3. The file in `security/manager/ssl/` that implements `nsNSSIOLayer` — the NSS I/O layer integration. 4. The file in `security/nss/lib/ssl/` that performs the actual TLS handshake (`sslsecur.c` or `ssl3con.c`). Report the file path and key class/function for each hop.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Perfect! I've successfully traced the Firefox TLS connection chain from the Necko networking layer to the NSS cryptographic layer. Here's a summary of what I found:

## TLS Connection Chain - Key Files and Functions

### 1. **HTTP Connection Layer** (netwerk/protocol/http/)
- **File**: `nsHttpConnection.h/.cpp`
- **Key Class**: `nsHttpConnection` - manages HTTP/HTTPS connections

### 2. **TLS Handshake Coordinator** (netwerk/protocol/http/)
- **File**: `TlsHandshaker.h/.cpp`
- **Key Methods**: 
  - `SetupSSL()` - initializes SSL for connections
  - `InitSSLParams()` - configures SSL parameters

### 3. **TLS Transport Layer** (netwerk/protocol/http/)
- **File**: `TLSTransportLayer.h/.cpp`
- **Class**: `TLSTransportLayer` - secondary TLS layer for HTTPS proxies

### 4. **SSL Socket Provider** (security/manager/ssl/)
- **File**: `nsSSLSocketProvider.cpp`
- **Method**: `NewSocket()` - creates SSL sockets

### 5. **NSS Bridge** (security/manager/ssl/)
- **File**: `nsNSSIOLayer.h/.cpp`
- **Key Class**: `nsSSLIOLayerHelpers` - bridges Necko to NSS
- **Key Functions**:
  - `nsSSLIOLayerNewSocket()` - creates TCP socket and wraps with SSL
  - `nsSSLIOLayerImportFD()` - imports socket into NSS via `SSL_ImportFD()`

### 6. **NSS Handshake Entry Points** (security/nss/lib/ssl/)
- **File**: `sslsecur.c`
- **Key Functions**:
  - `SSL_ForceHandshake()` - initiates TLS handshake
  - `ssl_Do1stHandshake()` - executes handshake state machine
  - `ssl_FinishHandshake()` - completes handshake

### 7. **TLS/SSL3 Protocol** (security/nss/lib/ssl/)
- **File**: `ssl3con.c`
- **Contains**: Complete TLS/SSL3 handshake implementation with state machine
